<p><b>Zoom Workplace</b> (commonly known and stylized as  <b>zoom</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary</a> <a href="/wiki/Videotelephony" title="Videotelephony">videotelephony</a> software program developed by <a href="/wiki/Zoom_Communications" title="Zoom Communications">Zoom Communications</a>. The free plan allows up to 100 concurrent participants, with a 40-minute time restriction. Users have the option to upgrade by subscribing to a paid plan, the highest of which supports up to 1,000 concurrent participants for meetings lasting up to 30 hours.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Zoom_Communications" title="Zoom Communications">Zoom Communications</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Zoom_Communications_Logo.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Zoom_Communications_Logo.svg/250px-Zoom_Communications_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="56" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Zoom_Communications_Logo.svg/500px-Zoom_Communications_Logo.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="225" /></a><figcaption>2014 logo</figcaption></figure>
<p>A beta version of Zoom that could host conferences with only up to 15 video participants was launched on August 21, 2012.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On January 25, 2013, version 1.0 of the program was released with an increase in the number of participants per conference to 25.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the end of its first month, Zoom had 400,000 users. By 2013, Zoom had more than one million users.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After the start of the COVID-19 pandemic, by February 2020, Zoom had gained 2.22 million users in 2020 – more users than it amassed in the entirety of 2019.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In March 2020, the Zoom app was downloaded 2.13 million times.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-guard1&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard1-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-tny&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tny-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, there was a major increase in the use of Zoom for <a href="/wiki/Remote_work" title="Remote work">remote work</a>, <a href="/wiki/Distance_education" title="Distance education">distance education</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and online social relations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-zoomnow&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zoomnow-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoom was one of the most downloaded mobile apps worldwide in 2020 with over 500 million downloads.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of April 2020, Zoom had more than 300 million daily meeting participants (calculated as the number of times someone joins a meeting, which can happen multiple times per day).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Features">Features</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Zoom One has six tiers: Basic, Pro, Business, Business Plus, Enterprise, and Enterprise Plus.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-busin&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-busin-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-cw&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cw-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoom is compatible with <a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, <a href="/wiki/ChromeOS" title="ChromeOS">ChromeOS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>. It is noted for its simple interface and usability, regardless of technological expertise.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-techrep&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techrep-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-nytdropbox&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytdropbox-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Features include one-on-one meetings, group video conferences, screen sharing, plugins, browser extensions, and the ability to record meetings and have them automatically transcribed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On some computers and operating systems, users are able to select a virtual background, which can be downloaded from different sites, to use as a backdrop behind themselves.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-wallst1&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wallst1-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Use of the platform is free for video conferences of up to 100 participants at once, with a 40-minute time limit. There is a 10-minute timeout period between free 40-minute meetings. For longer or larger conferences with more features, paid subscriptions are available. Features geared towards business conferences, such as Zoom Rooms, are also available.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-techrep&#95;22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techrep-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-wallst1&#95;25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wallst1-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-pricing&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pricing-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Up to 49 people can be seen on a <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">desktop</a> or <a href="/wiki/Laptop" title="Laptop">laptop</a> screen at once,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> up to 4 people per screen in <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a>, and up to 16 people per screen on <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a>.
</p><p>Zoom security features include password-protected meetings, user authentication, waiting rooms, locked meetings, disabling participant screen sharing, randomly generated IDs, and the ability for the host to remove disruptive attendees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of June 2020, Zoom began offering end-to-end encryption to business and enterprise users, with <a href="/wiki/AES_256" class="mw-redirect" title="AES 256">AES 256</a> <a href="/wiki/Galois/Counter_Mode" title="Galois/Counter Mode">GCM</a> encryption enabled for all users.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2020, Zoom added end-to-end encryption for free and paid users. It is available on all platforms, except for the official Zoom web client.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Zoom also offers a transcription service using <a href="/wiki/Otter.ai" title="Otter.ai">Otter.ai</a> software that allows businesses to store transcriptions of the Zoom meetings online and search them, including separating and labeling different speakers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2020, Zoom Rooms and Zoom Phone became available as <a href="/wiki/Hardware_as_a_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Hardware as a service">hardware as a service</a> products.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of July 2022, Zoom Phone is available for domestic telephone service in 47 countries, and the company has sold 3 million seats for the service.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-uct1&#95;34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uct1-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoom for Home, a category of products designed for home use, became available in August 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoom Phone Provider Exchange, which gives customers options for voice services, reaches more than 70 countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-uct1&#95;34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uct1-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In July 2022, an option was added on Zoom Phone to turn on end-to-end encryption during one-on-one calls between users on the same company account.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2020, Zoom added new accessibility features to make the app easier to use for those who are deaf, hard of hearing, or visually impaired. New features include the ability to move around video windows in gallery view, pin video windows to be spotlighted; improved keyboard shortcuts; new tools to adjust the size of closed captioning text; and sign language interpreters' windows can now sit directly next to the speaker.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2020 at Zoomtopia, Zoom's annual user conference, the company unveiled OnZoom, a virtual event marketplace with an integrated payment system where users can host and promote free or paid live events.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-digi&#95;38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digi-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With OnZoom, users will be able to schedule and host one-time events or event series for up to 1,000 attendees and sell tickets online.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-inc-1&#95;40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inc-1-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company also announced Zoom Apps, a feature integrating third-party apps so they can be used within the Zoom interface during meetings. The first such apps were expected to be available around the end of 2020, from companies including <a href="/wiki/Slack_Technologies" title="Slack Technologies">Slack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salesforce" title="Salesforce">Salesforce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dropbox_(service)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dropbox (service)">Dropbox</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-digi&#95;38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digi-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-inc-1&#95;40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inc-1-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatalog&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Qatalog (page does not exist)">Qatalog</a>. In October 2020, Zoom gave its users better security with an upgrade to end-to-end encryption for its online meetings network.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Also in October 2020, Zoom signed a carrier agreement with <a href="/wiki/BT_Global_Services" title="BT Global Services">Global BT Business</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to offer a fully managed Zoom Meetings service featuring a choice of connectivity and integration with its global voice network.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2021, Zoom added a "virtual receptionist" feature in the Kiosk Mode for Zoom Rooms. The feature was created to cater to in-person visitors at a business to interact in the lobby without physical contact.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On March 22, 2021, Zoom announced that it would start selling its videoconferencing technology as a <a href="/wiki/White-label_product" title="White-label product">white-label product</a>, so other companies can embed it in their own products, with the calls running over Zoom but not carrying the company's brand name.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2021, Zoom released Zoom Apps which integrated a marketplace of third-party applications such as <a href="/wiki/Dropbox" title="Dropbox">Dropbox Spaces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asana_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Asana (software)">Asana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SurveyMonkey" title="SurveyMonkey">SurveyMonkey</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2021, Zoom launched Focus Mode, designed for use in educational settings.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When active, the mode will hide participants' screens from each other (though they can see each other's names) while the host retains the ability to see everyone's camera stream or screen share.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The feature is available across all Zoom accounts, including free ones.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2021 at Zoomtopia, the company announced that end-to-end encryption would now be available as an upgrade for Zoom Phone users. The company also announced <a href="/wiki/Bring_your_own_key" class="mw-redirect" title="Bring your own key">bring your own key</a> (BYOK) (for users to manage their own encryption keys that Zoom cannot access or see), Verified Identity (a multi-factor authentication feature working through <a href="/wiki/Okta,_Inc." title="Okta, Inc.">Okta</a> that allows users to confirm the identity of meeting participants), and Video Engagement Center (for businesses to digitally interact with customers).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other updates include revamped virtual whiteboard features, including touchscreen whiteboards that can be digitized for remote participants, and improved collaboration between Zoom Meetings and Zoom Chat.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2021, the option to automatically generate closed captions in English for Zoom meetings was expanded to all accounts, including free ones. The feature had previously only been available for Premium users.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2022, Zoom added features including gesture recognition, a virtual whiteboard, and Zoom IQ for sales.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In February 2022, the company launched Zoom Contact Center, a cloud contact center optimized for video calls and integrated directly into Zoom.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2022, Zoom One, which brings together chat, phone, whiteboard, and video conferencing capabilities into a single offering, was launched.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cw&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cw-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-tt1&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tt1-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also in June 2022, Zoom opened its Zoom Apps developer program to all developers, via Zoom Apps SDK.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cw&#95;21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cw-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the release of Zoom One, the company offers video conferencing translation and captioning for 11 languages: English, simplified Chinese, Dutch, French, German, Italian, Japanese, Korean, Russian, Spanish, and Ukrainian. This feature is available with the Business Plus and Enterprise Plus plans.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-tt1&#95;59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tt1-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A version for <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV_(device)" title="Apple TV (device)">Apple TV</a> was released on December 1, 2023, which requires using an external iOS device as the user's camera.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-tvosverge&#95;5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tvosverge-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Usage">Usage</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Usage"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Zoom_Alma_Mater_Europaea.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Zoom_Alma_Mater_Europaea.jpg/330px-Zoom_Alma_Mater_Europaea.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="216" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Zoom_Alma_Mater_Europaea.jpg/500px-Zoom_Alma_Mater_Europaea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Zoom_Alma_Mater_Europaea.jpg/960px-Zoom_Alma_Mater_Europaea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1208" data-file-height="870" /></a><figcaption>In July 2020, using Zoom, the International Association of Constitutional Law and <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater_Europaea" title="Alma Mater Europaea">Alma Mater Europaea</a> organized the first round-the-clock and round-the-globe event that traveled through time zones.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Zoom is used by a variety of individuals and private and public organizations, including banks, schools,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> universities, healthcare providers, and government agencies,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and for ceremonies such as birthday parties,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> funeral services,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bar_and_bat_mitzvah" title="Bar and bat mitzvah">bar and bat mitzvah</a> services.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2020, Zoom formed a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> to create a virtual club where fans can go behind the scenes and take part in virtual activities through Zoom, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Grand_Prix" title="Hungarian Grand Prix">Hungarian Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> An article published in July 2020 in the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> noted a new real estate trend in San Francisco and Oakland where some listings include "Zoom rooms" with backdrops for Zoom calls.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Richard_Nelson_(playwright)" title="Richard Nelson (playwright)">Richard Nelson</a>'s play <i>What Do We Need to Talk About?</i> takes place on Zoom, with its main characters congregating online during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> using the platform. Written and directed by Nelson, it was commissioned by <a href="/wiki/The_Public_Theater" title="The Public Theater">The Public Theater</a> and premiered on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> on April 29, 2020, as a benefit performance. <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> called it "the first great original play of quarantine".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Oprah's Your Life in Focus: A Vision Forward</i> was a live virtual experience hosted by <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah Winfrey</a> on Zoom from May 16 through June 6, 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In Source Material's 2020 play, <i>In These Uncertain Times</i>, directed by Samantha Shay, characters communicate on Zoom.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The British <a href="/wiki/Found_footage_(film_technique)" title="Found footage (film technique)">found-footage</a> horror film <i><a href="/wiki/Host_(film)" title="Host (film)">Host</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Rob_Savage" title="Rob Savage">Rob Savage</a>, features a group of young people attempting to contact spirits through a remote séance on Zoom, and premiered on <a href="/wiki/Shudder_(streaming_service)" title="Shudder (streaming service)">Shudder</a> in July 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A live reading of <a href="/wiki/Kristoffer_Diaz" title="Kristoffer Diaz">Kristoffer Diaz</a>'s 2009 play <i><a href="/wiki/The_Elaborate_Entrance_of_Chad_Deity" title="The Elaborate Entrance of Chad Deity">The Elaborate Entrance of Chad Deity</a></i> over Zoom streamed on Play-PerView from August 15t to August 20, 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the 2021 film <i><a href="/wiki/Locked_Down_(2021_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Locked Down (2021 film)">Locked Down</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Doug_Liman" title="Doug Liman">Doug Liman</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chiwetel_Ejiofor" title="Chiwetel Ejiofor">Chiwetel Ejiofor</a>, characters communicate through Zoom conferences.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From July 3 to 4, 2020, the International Association of Constitutional Law and <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater_Europaea" title="Alma Mater Europaea">Alma Mater Europaea</a> used Zoom Webinar to conduct the first "round-the-clock and round-the-globe" event, featuring 52 speakers from 28 countries and several time zones.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Soon after, a format of conferences that "virtually travel the globe with the sun from East to West",<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> became common, some of them running for several days.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On September 17, 2020, a live table read of the script for the 1982 film <i><a href="/wiki/Fast_Times_at_Ridgemont_High" title="Fast Times at Ridgemont High">Fast Times at Ridgemont High</a></i> was hosted by <a href="/wiki/Dane_Cook" title="Dane Cook">Dane Cook</a>, with performers including <a href="/wiki/Brad_Pitt" title="Brad Pitt">Brad Pitt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Aniston" title="Jennifer Aniston">Jennifer Aniston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julia_Roberts" title="Julia Roberts">Julia Roberts</a>, original cast member <a href="/wiki/Sean_Penn" title="Sean Penn">Sean Penn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_McConaughey" title="Matthew McConaughey">Matthew McConaughey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shia_LaBeouf" title="Shia LaBeouf">Shia LaBeouf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Freeman" title="Morgan Freeman">Morgan Freeman</a> (who served as the narrator), <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel" title="Jimmy Kimmel">Jimmy Kimmel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ray_Liotta" title="Ray Liotta">Ray Liotta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a>, to raise money for the charity <a href="/wiki/Community_Organized_Relief_Effort" title="Community Organized Relief Effort">CORE</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The broadcast of the <a href="/wiki/72nd_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="72nd Primetime Emmy Awards">72nd Primetime Emmy Awards</a> on September 20, 2020, hosted by Jimmy Kimmel, featured nominees participating through Zoom.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On an alternate music video for the 2020 single "<a href="/wiki/Ice_Cream_(Blackpink_and_Selena_Gomez_song)" title="Ice Cream (Blackpink and Selena Gomez song)">Ice Cream</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Blackpink" title="Blackpink">Blackpink</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>, the artists appeared via Zoom from their homes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The series <i>Zoom Where It Happens</i>, airing on Zoom as a partnership between Zoom and Black female artists, launched in September 2020 with a virtual table read of an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Golden_Girls" title="The Golden Girls">The Golden Girls</a></i>, reimagined with an all-Black cast. The second episode featured an all-Black cast in a table read of an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Friends" title="Friends">Friends</a></i>, hosted by <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_Union" title="Gabrielle Union">Gabrielle Union</a> and featuring <a href="/wiki/Sterling_K._Brown" title="Sterling K. Brown">Sterling K. Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzo_Aduba" title="Uzo Aduba">Uzo Aduba</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
Familiarity with Zoom meetings in nation-state diplomatic and bureaucratic circles, partially due to the global <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, substantially contributed to the efficacy of the Western response to the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>During the 2024 US Presidential elections, the Democrats used Zoom to host mega-rallies to raise funds for Kamala Harris’ campaign. Zoom rallies attracted large numbers of viewers and raised millions of dollars. In one instance, a Zoom rally was disrupted when attendees exceeded the 100,000 cap for the Zoom corporate account and Zoom employees raised the group’s cap to 200,000 so the call could continue with such a large number of attendees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reception">Reception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Reception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Zoom has been criticized for "security lapses and poor design choices" that have resulted in heightened scrutiny of its software.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Lopez&#95;2020&#95;96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lopez_2020-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many of Zoom's issues "surround deliberate features designed to reduce friction in meetings", which <a href="/wiki/Citizen_Lab" title="Citizen Lab">Citizen Lab</a> found to "also, by design, reduce privacy or security".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-citlab&#95;97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citlab-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Donnell&#95;2020&#95;98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Donnell_2020-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In March 2020, <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Attorney_General" class="mw-redirect" title="New York State Attorney General">New York State Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Letitia_James" title="Letitia James">Letitia James</a> launched an inquiry into Zoom's privacy and security practices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nyag&#95;99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyag-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The inquiry was closed on May 7, 2020, with Zoom not admitting wrongdoing, but agreeing to take added security measures.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In April 2020, CEO Yuan apologized for the security issues, stating that some of the issues were a result of Zoom's having been designed for "large institutions with full IT support".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He noted that in December 2019, Zoom had a maximum of 10 million daily meeting participants, and in March 2020 the software had more than 200 million daily meeting participants, bringing the company increased challenges.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoom agreed to focus on data privacy and issue a transparency report.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In April 2020, the company released Zoom version 5.0, which addressed a number of the security and privacy concerns. It includes passwords by default, improved encryption, and a new security icon for meetings.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 2020, Zoom added support for <a href="/wiki/Two-factor_authentication" class="mw-redirect" title="Two-factor authentication">two-factor authentication</a> to its desktop and mobile apps; the security feature was previously Web-only.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of April 2020, businesses, schools, and government entities who have restricted or prohibited the use of Zoom on their networks include <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Siemens&#95;110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Siemens-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Defence_Force" title="Australian Defence Force">Australian Defence Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="German Ministry of Foreign Affairs">German Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Home_Affairs_(India)" title="Ministry of Home Affairs (India)">Indian Ministry of Home Affairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Education" title="New York City Department of Education">New York City Department of Education</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-who&#95;111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May 2020, the New York City Department of Education lifted their ban on Zoom after the company addressed security and privacy concerns.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Privacy">Privacy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Privacy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Zoom has been criticized for its privacy and corporate data sharing policies, as well as for enabling video hosts to potentially violate the privacy of those participating in their calls.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, a <a href="/wiki/Motherboard_(website)" class="mw-redirect" title="Motherboard (website)">Motherboard</a> article found that the company's <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> app was sending device analytics data to <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> on startup, regardless of whether a Facebook account was being used with the service, and without disclosing it to the user.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoom responded that it had been made aware of the issue and patched the app to remove the <a href="/wiki/Software_development_kit" title="Software development kit">SDK</a> after learning that it was collecting unnecessary device data. The company stated that the SDK was only collecting information on the user's device specifications (such as model names and operating system versions) in order to optimize its service and that it was not collecting personal information.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-wallst1&#95;25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wallst1-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the same month, Zoom was sued by a user in <a href="/wiki/U.S._Federal_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Federal Court">U.S. Federal Court</a> for illegally and secretly disclosing personal data to third parties, including Facebook.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoom responded that it "has never sold user data in the past and has no intention of selling users' data going forward".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2020, a Zoom information gathering feature was found that automatically sent user names and email addresses to <a href="/wiki/LinkedIn" title="LinkedIn">LinkedIn</a>, allowing some participants to surreptitiously access LinkedIn profile data about other users without their express consent.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Soon after, the companies disabled their integration.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> announced that it was looking into Zoom's privacy practices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The FTC alleged in a complaint<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FTC-complaint&#95;125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FTC-complaint-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that since at least 2016, "Zoom maintained the cryptographic keys that could allow Zoom to access the content of its customers' meetings, did not provide advertised end-to-end encryption, falsely claimed <a href="/wiki/Health_Insurance_Portability_and_Accountability_Act" title="Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act">HIPAA</a> compliance, installed the ZoomOpener webserver without adequate consent, did not uninstall the web server after uninstalling the Zoom App, and secured its Zoom Meetings with a lower level of encryption than promised."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On November 9, 2020, a settlement was reached, requiring the company to stop misrepresenting security features, create an <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">information security</a> program, obtain biannual assessments by a third party, and implement additional security measures.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FTC-agreement&#95;127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FTC-agreement-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Security">Security</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Security"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Vulnerabilities">Vulnerabilities</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Vulnerabilities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In November 2018, a security vulnerability was discovered that allowed a remote unauthenticated attacker to spoof <a href="/wiki/User_Datagram_Protocol" title="User Datagram Protocol">UDP</a> messages that allowed the attacker to remove attendees from meetings, spoof messages from users, or hijack shared screens.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company released fixes shortly after the vulnerability was discovered.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In July 2019, security researcher Jonathan Leitschuh disclosed a <a href="/wiki/Zero-day_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zero-day (computing)">zero-day</a> vulnerability allowing any website to force a <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a> user to join a Zoom call, with their <a href="/wiki/Video_camera" title="Video camera">video camera</a> activated, without the user's permission.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Attempts to uninstall the Zoom client on macOS would prompt the software to re-install automatically in the background using a hidden web server that was set up on the machine during the first installation so that it remains active even after attempting to remove the client. After receiving public criticism, Zoom removed the vulnerability and the hidden webserver to allow complete uninstallation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In April 2020, security researchers found vulnerabilities where <a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a> users' <a href="/wiki/Credential#Information_technology" title="Credential">credentials</a> could be exposed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another vulnerability allowing unprompted access to cameras and microphones was made public.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoom issued a fix in April 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Motherboard reported that there were two Zoom <a href="/wiki/Zero-day_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zero-day (computing)">zero-days</a> for macOS and Windows respectively, selling for $500,000, on April 15, 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Security bug brokers were selling access to Zoom security flaws that could allow remote access into users' computers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nytdropbox&#95;23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytdropbox-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Hackers also put up over 500,000 Zoom user names and passwords for sale on the <a href="/wiki/Dark_web" title="Dark web">dark web</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nytdropbox&#95;23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytdropbox-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In response to the multitude of security and privacy issues found, Zoom began a comprehensive security plan, which included consulting with Luta Security, Trail of Bits, former <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> CSO <a href="/wiki/Alex_Stamos" title="Alex Stamos">Alex Stamos</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> global lead of privacy technology Lea Kissner, BishopFox, the <a href="/wiki/NCC_Group" title="NCC Group">NCC Group</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a> cryptographer <a href="/wiki/Matthew_D._Green" title="Matthew D. Green">Matthew D. Green</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On April 20, 2020, the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Dropbox_(service)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dropbox (service)">Dropbox</a> engineers had traced Zoom's security vulnerabilities back over two years, pushing Zoom to address such issues more quickly, and paying top hackers to find problems with Zoom's software. In the same article, the <i>New York Times</i> noted that security researchers have praised Zoom for improving its response times, and for quickly patching recent bugs and removing features that could have privacy risks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nytdropbox&#95;23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytdropbox-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-wallst1&#95;25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wallst1-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In a blog post on April 1, 2020, CEO Yuan announced a 90-day freeze on releasing new features, to focus on fixing privacy and security issues within the platform.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-wallst2&#95;140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wallst2-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  On July 1, 2020, at the end of the freeze, the company stated it had released 100 new safety features over the 90-day period. Those efforts include end-to-end encryption for all users, turning on meeting passwords by default, giving users the ability to choose which data centers calls are routed from, consulting with security experts, forming a CISO council, an improved bug bounty program, and working with third parties to help test security. Yuan also stated that Zoom would be sharing a transparency report later in 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On November 16, 2020, Zoom announced a new security feature to combat disruptions during a session. The new feature was said to be a default for all free and paid users and made available on the Zoom clients for <a href="/wiki/MacBook" title="MacBook">Mac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>, as well as Zoom mobile apps.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On August 12, 2022, <a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired magazine</a> reported on three separate security vulnerabilities discovered by security researcher Patrick Wardle affecting the Zoom <a href="/wiki/Macintosh_operating_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Macintosh operating systems">Mac OS</a> desktop app. The vulnerabilities allowed an attacker who already had access to the Mac device to perform a <a href="/wiki/Privilege_escalation" title="Privilege escalation">privilege escalation</a> attack by installing malicious code using the app's auto-update feature, thereby giving them full control over the victim's device.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Zoombombing">Zoombombing</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Zoombombing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Zoombombing" title="Zoombombing">Zoombombing</a></div>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Zoombombing" title="Zoombombing">Zoombombing</a>" is a phenomenon where uninvited participants join a meeting to cause disruption.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In July 2019, security researcher Sam Jadali uncovered the <a href="/wiki/DataSpii" title="DataSpii">DataSpii</a> leak.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This catastrophic leak was facilitated by a marketing intelligence company known as Nacho Analytics (NA), which provided its members access to the URLs of real-time Zoom meetings of firms such as Oracle, Dell, Walmart, Uber, UCLA and Capital One.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> NA's dissemination of meeting URLs enabled its members to Zoombomb these meetings. In April 2020, Zoom increased its default security settings to mitigate Zoombombing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-techrep&#95;22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techrep-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company also created a new "report a user to Zoom" button, intended to catch those behind Zoombombing attacks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Encryption_practices">Encryption practices</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Encryption practices"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Zoom encrypts its public data streams, using <a href="/wiki/TLS_1.2" class="mw-redirect" title="TLS 1.2">TLS 1.2</a> with AES-256 (<a href="/wiki/Advanced_Encryption_Standard" title="Advanced Encryption Standard">Advanced Encryption Standard</a>) to protect <a href="/wiki/Signaling_(telecommunications)" title="Signaling (telecommunications)">signaling</a>, and AES-128 to protect <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streaming media</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Security researchers and reporters have criticized the company for its lack of transparency and poor encryption practices. Zoom initially claimed to use "<a href="/wiki/End-to-end_encryption" title="End-to-end encryption">end-to-end encryption</a>" in its marketing materials,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but later clarified it meant "from Zoom end point to Zoom end point" (meaning effectively between Zoom servers and Zoom clients), which <i><a href="/wiki/The_Intercept" title="The Intercept">The Intercept</a></i> described as misleading and "dishonest".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alex_Stamos" title="Alex Stamos">Alex Stamos</a>, a Zoom advisor who was formerly security chief at <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, noted that a lack of end-to-end encryption is common in such products, as it is also true of <a href="/wiki/Google_Hangouts" title="Google Hangouts">Google Hangouts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Teams" title="Microsoft Teams">Microsoft Teams</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Webex" class="mw-redirect" title="Cisco Webex">Cisco Webex</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cnbc1&#95;156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc1-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On May 7, 2020, Zoom announced that it had acquired <a href="/wiki/Keybase" title="Keybase">Keybase</a>, a company specializing in end-to-end encryption, as part of an effort to strengthen its security practices moving forward.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-wiredkeybase&#95;157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiredkeybase-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later that month, Zoom published a document for peer review, detailing its plans to ultimately bring end-to-end encryption to the software.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2020, Citizen Lab researchers discovered that a single, server-generated AES-128 key is being shared between all participants in <a href="/wiki/Block_cipher_mode_of_operation#Electronic_codebook_(ECB)" title="Block cipher mode of operation">ECB mode</a>, which is deprecated due to its pattern-preserving characteristics of the ciphertext.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During test calls between participants in Canada and United States, the key was provisioned from servers located in mainland China where they are subject to the <a href="/wiki/China_Internet_Security_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="China Internet Security Law">China Internet Security Law</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-citlab&#95;97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citlab-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On June 3, 2020, Zoom announced that users on their free tier will not have access to <a href="/wiki/End-to-end_encryption" title="End-to-end encryption">end-to-end encryption</a> so that they could cooperate with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> and law enforcement.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later, they said that they do not "proactively monitor meeting content".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On June 17, 2020, the company reversed course and announced that free users would have access to end-to-end encryption after all.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On September 7, 2020, cryptography researcher <a href="/wiki/Nadim_Kobeissi" title="Nadim Kobeissi">Nadim Kobeissi</a> accused Zoom's security team of failing to credit his open-source protocol analysis research software, Verifpal, with being instrumental during the design phase of Zoom's new encryption protocol, as described in their whitepaper published in June 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Kobeissi published a week's worth of conversations with Zoom's security leadership in support of his claim, including Max Krohn, which included eight Verifpal models that Zoom's team asked for feedback on, promises of a citation to credit Kobeissi for his contributions and an admission that the Verifpal citation was pulled from the whitepaper at the last moment for unspecified reasons. Kobeissi also linked to a tweet by Zoom security consultant Lea Kissner which he described as a public <a href="/wiki/Character_assassination" title="Character assassination">character assassination</a> attempt issued in response to his repeated requests to have his work cited in the research paper published by Zoom.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Data_routing">Data routing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Data routing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Zoom admitted that some calls in early April 2020 and prior were mistakenly routed through servers in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>, prompting some governments and businesses to cease their usage of Zoom.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company later announced that data of free users outside of China would "never be routed through China" and that paid subscribers will be able to customize which data center regions they want to use. The company has data centers in Europe, Asia, North America, and Latin America.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Regulatory_issues">Regulatory issues</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoom_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Regulatory issues"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In August 2021, the Data Protection regulatory body in Hamburg, Germany, ruled that Zoom was operating in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in breach of the <a href="/wiki/General_Data_Protection_Regulation" title="General Data Protection Regulation">General Data Protection Regulation</a> (GDPR). This is due to the fact that, as per the <i><a href="/wiki/Schrems_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Schrems II">Schrems II</a></i> ruling, data that is transferred out of the EU must be protected as the GDPR requires. The data gathered by Zoom was being sent to the United States.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
